[8:0:200,329] 3845 San Diego River Conservancy 

[8:1:58,350] The mission of the San Diego River Conservancy is to achieve the goals of the San Diego River Conservancy Act by 

[8:2:58,359] implementing five major programs: Land Conservation, Recreation and Education, Preserve Natural/Cultural Resources, 

[8:3:58,368] Water Quality and Natural Flood Conveyance, and Organizational Capacity and Reach. This mission will be accomplished in 

[8:4:58,377] part by building, with our partners, a San Diego River Park and hiking trail stretching from the headwaters in Julian to the 

[8:5:58,386] Pacific Ocean. These programs foster collaboration among governments and nonprofit organizations, and leverage grant

[11:0:58,444] 3220 - SIERRA NEVADA CONSERVANCY PROGRAM 

[12:0:58,462] Established pursuant to Chapter 726, Statutes of 2004, the Conservancy is authorized to: 

[12:1:68,480] Provide increased opportunities for tourism and recreation. 

[13:0:58,478] • 

[13:1:58,487] • 

[13:2:58,496] • 

[13:3:58,505] • 

[13:4:58,514] • 

[13:5:58,523] • 

[13:6:58,532] • 

[14:0:68,489] Protect, conserve, and restore the region's physical, cultural, archaeological, historical, and living resources. 

[14:1:68,498] Aid in the preservation of working landscapes. 

[14:2:68,507] Reduce the risk of natural disasters, such as wildfires. 

[14:3:68,516] Protect and improve water and air quality. 

[15:0:68,525] Assist the regional economy through the operation of the Conservancy's program. 

[15:1:68,534] Undertake efforts to enhance public use and enjoyment of lands owned by the public. 

[16:0:58,552] In support of these programs, the Conservancy facilitates collaborative planning efforts with local and regional governments, 

[16:1:58,561] community groups and interested parties, provides technical assistance, and initiates and funds projects to identify and fill 

[16:2:58,570] critical needs in the Sierra Nevada region.

[7:0:194,252] 3860 Department of Water Resources 

[7:1:58,273] The Department of Water Resources protects, conserves, develops, and manages California's water. The Department 

[7:2:58,282] evaluates existing water resources, forecasts future water needs and explores future potential solutions to meet ever-

[7:3:58,291] growing needs for personal use, irrigation, industry, recreation, power generation, and fish and wildlife. The Department also 

[7:4:58,300] works to prevent and minimize flood damage, oversee the safety of dams, and educate the public about the importance of 

[7:5:58,309] water and its efficient use. 

[8:0:58,327] Because the Department's programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has a capital outlay program 

[8:1:58,336] to support this need. For the specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[10:0:58,186] Totals, Budget Adjustments   $112,802   $785,013   -45.0   $36,492   $78,871   -305.2
[11:0:58,218] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[12:0:58,245] 3230 - CONTINUING FORMULATION OF THE CALIFORNIA WATER PLAN 

[13:0:58,263] The California Water Plan is the state's strategic plan for the efficient use, management and development of the state's 

[13:1:58,272] water resources. The Plan is updated every five years and provides a framework for water managers, legislators, and the 

[13:2:58,281] public to consider options and make decisions regarding California's water future. The Plan evaluates current and future 

[13:3:58,290] water conditions, challenges and opportunities. It presents basic data and information on California's water resources 

[13:4:58,299] including water supply evaluations and assessments of existing and future agricultural, urban, and environmental water 

[13:5:58,308] uses. The Plan identifies and evaluates multiple future scenarios and over 30 resource management strategies such as 

[13:6:58,317] conservation, recycling, desalination, transfers, storage, conveyance, water quality, watershed management, ecosystem 

[13:7:58,326] restoration, and urban land use management to help meet future demands in light of uncertainties and unexpected 

[13:8:58,335] catastrophic events. This program also identifies ways for the state to: (1) help local agencies and governments prepare 

[13:9:58,344] integrated regional water management plans on a watershed basis and diversify their regional water portfolios to ensure 

[13:10:58,353] sustainable water uses, reliable water supplies, better water quality, environmental stewardship, efficient urban 

[14:0:58,362] development, protection of agriculture, and a strong economy, (2) help cities, counties and local agencies prepare a Water 

[14:1:58,371] Element for their General Plans, Urban Water Management Plans and Agricultural Water Management Plans, and (3) help 

[14:2:58,380] local agencies and tribal governments improve coordination between water and land use planning. 

[15:0:58,398] 3240 - IMPLEMENTATION OF THE STATE WATER RESOURCES DEVELOPMENT SYSTEM 

[16:0:58,416] The State Water Project is a water storage and delivery system that consists of 34 storage facilities (reservoirs and lakes), 

[16:1:58,425] 20 pumping plants, 4 pumping-generating plants, 5 hydroelectric power plants, and over 700 miles of conveyance (canals, 

[16:2:58,434] pipelines, and tunnels). The Project provides water to over 25 million Californians and 750,000 acres of irrigated farmland. 

[17:0:58,452] The Department plans, designs, constructs, operates, maintains, and manages State Water Project facilities which provide 

[17:1:58,461] water to facilities located from Plumas County to Riverside County. 

[18:0:58,479] The Delta Habitat Conservation and Conveyance Program is charged with improving the Delta ecosystem and ensuring 

[18:1:58,488] water supply reliability in a safe, timely, and cost effective manner. This includes development of the Bay Delta Conservation 

[18:2:58,497] Plan, project specific conservation measures, and the Environmental Impact Report and Environmental Impact Statement. 

[19:0:58,515] 3245 - PUBLIC SAFETY AND PREVENTION OF DAMAGE 

[20:0:58,533] This program supports the California Water Action Plan by protecting life and property from damage by floods, ensures 

[20:1:58,542] proper construction and maintenance of jurisdictional dams and levees, and provides loans for the construction. Activities 

[20:2:58,551] include assessing the state and regional investment needs to reduce risk, preventive floodplain management to discourage 

[20:3:58,560] unwise use of areas subject to flooding, protection of floodplains, issuance of flood warnings, operation of flood control 

[20:4:58,569] facilities, coordination and supervision of flood fight activities, and annual levee and flood channel maintenance and 

[21:0:58,578] inspection in cooperation with other local, state, and federal partner agencies. This program also buys land, easements, and 

[21:1:58,587] rights-of-way for federal flood control projects and supervises the design and construction of new dams and periodic 

[21:2:58,596] inspection and reevaluation of all existing jurisdictional dams for proper operation and maintenance. Fiscal oversight and 

[21:3:58,605] coordination activities associated with the Disaster Preparedness and Flood Prevention Bond Act of 2006 are administered 

[21:4:58,614] under this program. The program also reviews federal dam projects in coordination with federal and other state agencies 

[21:5:58,623] with regard to dam safety. 

[22:0:58,641] 3250 - CENTRAL VALLEY FLOOD PROTECTION BOARD 

[23:0:58,659] The Central Valley Flood Protection Board has regulatory authority over the State Plan of Flood Control facilities (SPFC), 

[23:1:58,668] designated floodways and regulated streams in the Central Valley. The Board regulates encroachments on the system by 

[23:2:58,677] issuing permits and initiating enforcement action when necessary to maintain the integrity of the levees and floodways that 

[23:3:58,686] protect the valley's people and property. The Board manages the state's portfolio of real property held by the Sacramento-

[23:4:58,695] San Joaquin Drainage District. The Board serves as the non-federal sponsor to the United States Army Corps of Engineers 

[23:5:58,704] on large joint state-federal levee improvement projects and assists the more than one hundred local maintaining agencies 

[23:6:58,713] that operate and maintain the SPFC. The Board conducts regular public meetings, workshops and tours, providing a public 

[23:7:58,722] forum for stakeholders. 

[24:0:58,745] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[2:0:58,82] 3255 - SERVICES 

[3:0:58,100] This program provides technical support within the Department and expertise in the fields of water resources planning, 

[3:1:58,109] development and management; watermaster services; scientific analyses performed by DWR's chemical laboratory; 

[3:2:58,118] information technology; and mapping, surveying and engineering services for other agencies. 

[3:3:58,136] 3260 - CALIFORNIA ENERGY RESOURCES SCHEDULING 

[4:0:58,154] For a limited period of time, this program purchased electric power on behalf of the state's investor-owned utilities. Beginning 

[4:1:58,163] January 1, 2003, the utility companies resumed responsibility for purchasing power from the spot market. The utilities, 

[4:2:58,172] however, continued to receive power from the Department's long-term energy contracts with energy suppliers, under which 

[4:3:58,181] the Department retains legal and financial responsibility. All energy contracts signed by the Department have now expired 

[4:4:58,190] or were terminated. However, litigation continues against some of the counterparties to these contracts. Additionally, the 

[4:5:58,199] Department retains the legal and financial responsibility for administering $4.621 billion in revenue bonds issued to repay the 

[4:6:58,208] General Fund for money borrowed for power purchases during the energy crisis and funding of reserve accounts necessary 

[4:7:58,217] to maintain an investment grade credit rating associated with the revenue bonds.

[8:0:58,403] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW 

[9:0:58,421] The Department of Water Resources has two major infrastructure programs: the State Water Project and the flood control 

[9:1:58,430] system in the Central Valley. The State Water Project is a water storage and delivery system that consists of 34 storage 

[9:2:58,439] facilities, reservoirs, and lakes, 20 pumping plants, 4 pumping-generating plants, 5 hydroelectric power plants, and over 700 

[9:3:58,448] miles of canals, pipelines, and tunnels. The Project provides water to 25 million Californians and 750,000 acres of irrigated 

[9:4:58,457] farmland. The Project also provides recreational opportunities to approximately 6 million visitors annually at 15 separate 

[9:5:58,466] reservoir-based facilities as well as public fishing access to much of the Aqueduct. Existing flood control infrastructure in the 

[9:6:58,475] Central Valley consists of 1,595 miles of levees, 348,000 acres of channels and floodways, over 800,000 linear feet of bank 

[9:7:58,484] protection, over 60 mitigation and environmental restoration sites, and 55 various flood control structures including dams, 

[9:8:58,493] weirs, pumping plants, diversion structures, gate structures, and drop structures. In general, these facilities provide more 

[9:9:58,502] flood protection in urbanized areas and less in agricultural areas.

[3:0:158,149] 3875 Sacramento-San Joaquin Delta Conservancy 

[3:1:58,170] The mission of the Sacramento-San Joaquin Delta Conservancy is to support efforts that advance both environmental 

[4:0:58,179] protection and the economic well-being of Delta residents in a complementary manner. The Conservancy's activities include 

[4:1:58,188] protecting and enhancing habitat and habitat restoration; protecting and preserving Delta agriculture and working 

[4:2:58,197] landscapes; providing increased opportunities for tourism and recreation; promoting Delta legacy communities and 

[4:3:58,206] economic vitality in the Delta; increasing the resilience of the Delta to the effects of natural disasters such as floods and 

[4:4:58,215] earthquakes; protecting and improving water quality; assisting the Delta regional economy; identifying priority projects and 

[4:5:58,224] initiatives for which funding is needed; conducting activities to protect, conserve, and restore the region's physical, 

[4:6:58,233] agricultural, cultural, historical, and living resources; assisting local entities in the implementation of their habitat 

[5:0:58,242] conservation plans and natural community conservation plans; facilitating protection and safe harbor agreements under the 

[5:1:58,251] federal Endangered Species Act of 1973 and the California Endangered Species Act for adjacent land owners and local 

[5:2:58,260] public agencies; and promoting environmental education. The Conservancy acts as a primary state agency to implement 

[5:3:58,269] ecosystem restoration in the Delta and supports efforts that advance environmental protection and the economic well-being 

[5:4:58,278] of the Delta residents.

[6:0:210,264] 3885 Delta Stewardship Council 

[6:1:58,285] Established in 2009 by the Delta Reform Act, the mission of the Delta Stewardship Council, through a seven-member board, 

[6:2:58,294] is to further the state's coequal goals of providing a more reliable water supply for California and protecting, restoring, and 

[6:3:58,303] enhancing the Sacramento-San Joaquin Delta ecosystem. The coequal goals are to be achieved in a manner that protects 

[6:4:58,312] and enhances the unique cultural, recreational, natural resource, and agricultural values of the Delta. In 2013, the Council 

[6:5:58,321] adopted a legally enforceable Delta Plan to further the coequal goals and guide state and local agency activities related to 

[6:6:58,330] the Delta. Under state law, agencies are required to coordinate their actions pursuant to the Delta Plan with the Council and 

[6:7:58,339] the other relevant agencies. The Council is informed by scientific input from the Delta Science Program and the Delta 

[6:8:58,348] Independent Science Board. The mission of the Delta Science Program is to provide the best possible unbiased scientific 

[6:9:58,357] information to inform water and environmental decisionmaking in the Delta.
